Sentence for Illegally Carrying Opium Residue

Five Months Imprisonment, Three Years Probation

Zhang Yinkui from Tongzhou was found carrying a bag of opium residue weighing 125 pounds at around 8:20 AM on the 6th of this month near the intersection of Tiantong Road and North Sichuan Road. He was stopped and apprehended by Chinese detective Tang Guangfu. Zhang claimed that he worked as a rickshaw puller at the Jizhitang Pharmacy at No. 236 North Shanxi Road and that the opium residue was purchased from a certain Jia at Sanguantang Lane, Huaji Road, at the direction of his boss, Li Bingchen, for use in making pills. Detective Tang went to the pharmacy to investigate, but the boss, Mr. Li, was not there, so he was taken to the Hongkou Police Station and sent to the First Special District Court for detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiefei continued the trial in the Third Criminal Court. Mr. Zhang Shizhu, lawyer for the Public Works Department, presented the case and requested an investigation of the defendant's confession. The defendant stated that he intended to bring the opium residue back to his hometown to grow trees, as he was deceived by others, and asked for leniency. The duty lawyer stated that the defendant's monthly wage at the pharmacy was only 12 yuan, and he relied on it to support his family. He asked the court to consider this. Judge Xiao sentenced Zhang Yinkui to five months imprisonment, suspended for three years, and confiscated the opium residue. Mr. Zhang, lawyer for the Public Works Department, did not appeal, and Zhang was released immediately.

Hengjiu Bank Sues Zhou Weishi for Not Settling 10,000 Yuan Mortgage

Yesterday, the Case Was Studied Once, Resulting in a Continued Hearing with Witnesses

Zhou Weishi, a wealthy Suzhou merchant in his sixties who owns the famous Zhou Gengji Accounting Firm and resides at No. 379 Paofengting Road, was recently sued by Hengjiu Bank in the First Special District Court for failing to settle a 10,000 yuan mortgage. Yesterday, Judge Xu Fuji summoned him to the Fourth Civil Court. The lawyer representing Hengjiu Bank presented the case, stating that the defendant had mortgaged 10,000 yuan to the plaintiff under the name of Zhou Gengji for a term of six months. After repeated extensions, the term expired at the end of October of this year, but the defendant still failed to repay the debt, hence the lawsuit. The plaintiff requested a judgment ordering full repayment and interest at a rate of 8% per month until the date of enforcement, and also requested permission for provisional execution, as Zhou was on the verge of bankruptcy with debts of approximately 500,000 to 600,000 yuan. Without provisional execution, it would be difficult to recover the debt. Zhou's lawyer argued that the defendant owed a total of 550,000 yuan to various creditors, who formed a group and appointed Ruichang Bank as their representative. The defendant entered into a trust agreement with Ruichang, using the land in Chun Geng Li as collateral. The agreement was certified by lawyer Huang Yiyan. One of the members of the plaintiff group broke away and filed a separate lawsuit, which was illegal and should be dismissed. The court summoned lawyer Huang to testify about the agreement. Judge Xu then announced that the hearing would be postponed for further examination with witnesses.

Suspected of Smuggling Japanese Gold Bars, Zhou Yonghua Arrested

Police Arrested Zhou Upon Arrival in Shanghai at the Request of the Japanese Consulate

Zhou Yonghua, a native of Ningbo, residing at No. 593 Tangshan Road, Hongkou, is currently a Hong Bang tailor, 35 years old. Zhou was arrested at 3:45 AM yesterday on suspicion of smuggling gold bars from Japan to Shanghai by Chinese detective Zhang Youming and Western detective Wall from the Huishan Police Station, taken into custody, and then sent to the Fifth Criminal Court of the First Special Court at 9:30 AM, requesting detention. According to police lawyer Jiang Baolian, last night, the Japanese Consulate sent officials to the police station to report that a Chinese person was carrying gold bars and gold coins from Japan on the Changxing Company's Asia Empress ship, which was scheduled to dock at the Gonghexing Wharf this morning, requesting investigation. The police dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to the Asia Empress ship at the Gonghexing Wharf at 0:30 AM yesterday, arrested Zhou Yonghua, and searched his person, discovering a specially made vest with multiple small pockets in the front and back. They found ten gold bars, eighteen ten-yuan gold coins, and one five-yuan gold coin, worth a total of 15,000 yuan, which were confiscated and presented as evidence. They requested detention for further investigation. Furthermore, Nagaoka Takeo, representative of the Japanese Consulate, submitted a statement that the information was notified by the Japanese authorities in Japan to the Japanese Consulate and relayed to the police. Questioned, Zhou Yonghua stated that he went to Japan to sell cloth and returned to Shanghai from Kobe on the ship. A certain Lao Wang on the same ship gave him the gold bars to bring to Shanghai and promised a reward of 20 yuan. Judge Zhan Liangce reviewed the confession and ordered Zhou Yonghua to be detained for seven days for further questioning.

Fire at Old Baidu Street

At around 9:00 AM yesterday morning, a sudden fire broke out at the Wanlong Fresh Meat Shop at No. 119 Old Baidu Street, Nanshi District. The fire quickly spread, piercing through the roof and spreading to neighboring shops such as the Yumao Fried Goods Shop and the Yuanxing Barber Shop. Fortunately, firefighters from various districts arrived and connected pumps to extinguish the fire, which was brought under control after about an hour. The fire destroyed three buildings. The Sixteen Pu Branch Police Station dispatched officers to investigate and detain the arsonist for questioning.

Wang Haixi Severely Injured in Knife Attack

Wang Haixi, a 44-year-old native of Yancheng, residing at No. 20 Fushan Lane, Tiantong'an Road, was previously a detective's assistant and is now unemployed, specializing in collecting apprentices at Xiangyan Bridge and other places. Every day, Wang would go to the Xinxin Teahouse at Xiangyan Bridge to drink tea. At around 8:30 AM yesterday, Wang went to the teahouse as usual. Before he had been sitting for long, a person carrying a sharp axe rushed upstairs and, without asking any questions, struck Wang three times, seriously injuring his head and causing him to faint and fall to the ground. The assailant, seeing his objective achieved, attempted to flee, but fortunately, patrolling police had arrived and apprehended him. He confessed that his name was Yang Fudi and that he was also Wang's apprentice. Yang's lover had recently disappeared suddenly, and he suspected that Wang was responsible, so he committed the act. The police station, believing that the case required further investigation, detained the assailant and sent Wang Haixi to the hospital for treatment.

Wife Seeks Divorce After Husband's Three-Year Absence

Husband Never Returns

Huang Sanbao, a young woman from Haimen, 20 years old, recently filed a lawsuit in the District Court against her husband, Zhou Ayuan, for abandonment and absence for more than three years, requesting a divorce. Yesterday morning, Judge Gan heard the case. Huang Sanbao stated that she was 20 years old and married Zhou Ayuan at the age of 17 under the arrangement of her parents. Zhou Ayuan was originally a tea and snack shop worker but suddenly became unemployed. In April of that year, after marrying him, she lived with him for only two months until the landlord demanded rent. Zhou Ayuan went out to find a way to raise the money but never returned. It has been three years since then. She hired a lawyer to publish a notice in the newspaper, but there was no response. Therefore, she is requesting a divorce to find a way out. Witness Zhao testified that Huang Sanbao used to live with her at No. 2 Tai'an Lane, Tai'an Street, Ximen. Her husband did leave after being asked for rent and has not returned. The judge verified the statements and ordered that Huang Sanbao's parents be summoned to court for further questioning.

Wrestling Performance Tonight, Huang Bochang vs. Miha, 8:30 PM at St. George's Garden

Mr. Huang Bochang, a Chinese wrestling master, fought against Philippine wrestler Aqinainedu at St. George's Garden on Route Doumer two weeks ago and won 3-2, making a name for himself. Tonight, he will fight against Indian master Miha, which will be even more exciting. Miha weighs ten pounds more than Huang and has great physical strength, but Huang has fought hundreds of battles, so he still has a chance of winning. Huang is from Guangzhou. At the age of seven, he followed his parents to the United States to study dentistry. Later, due to economic reasons, he gave up his studies and specialized in wrestling. He became famous for a while and became a master of American wrestling. Tonight, there will be a total of six wrestling matches, each lasting ten minutes. At the same time, there will be other exciting programs such as wrestling and boxing. Tickets are priced at 2 yuan, 3 yuan, and 4 yuan. Reservations can be made at Qimei Western Restaurant at No. 133 Nanjing Road until 8:30 PM. After 7:00 PM, reservations can be made at St. George's Garden.

Key Points of American Wrestling

American wrestling has different rules than Chinese wrestling. Here are some key points for the audience's reference: (1) If both shoulders touch the ground for three seconds, it is considered a "fall"; (2) Lifting the opponent into the air and throwing them to the ground, causing them to faint for ten seconds, is considered a "fall"; (3) Pressing on the opponent's tendons or striking any part of the opponent's body with an elbow, causing them to be unable to endure and voluntarily surrender, is considered a "fall"; (4) Throwing the opponent out of the ring and not returning within twenty seconds is considered a "fall". Victory is achieved by consecutively or first knocking down the opponent twice.

Thirteen-Mile Long-Distance Run, Announcement of Participant Guidelines

Registration Deadline: 25th

The marathon long-distance race initiated by the Chinese Marathon Promotion Association is scheduled to start on New Year's Day next year at the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Avenue Haig. The total distance is thirteen miles. Since registration began on November 21st of last month, participation has been enthusiastic, with over 130 registrants. The association yesterday announced three guidelines for participants: (1) Participants must fill in their detailed address when registering; otherwise, they must supplement it within days so that number tags can be collected on the 27th. (2) Participants in the long-distance race must be at least sixteen years old and confident in their physical ability to run long distances. Do not overestimate yourself, as it may be harmful. (3) The registration deadline is the 25th of this month. If it rains during the competition, it will be postponed. As for trophies and prizes, the Hua De Light Bulb Factory has donated three silver cups. Jiangxi Province Implements a Hundred Industries Education Plan. Using Educational Methods to Improve the Skills of Workers in All Industries and Instill Basic Knowledge of Citizenship

In view of the current decline in all industries and economic recession in Jiangxi Province, the province has launched education for all industries to improve the knowledge and skills of workers in all industries, increase work efficiency, and promote the prosperity of all industries and economic recovery. The province has formulated and promulgated the Outline of the Implementation Plan for Education in All Industries and the Organizational Regulations for the Committee for the Implementation of Education in All Industries. The current committee was officially established in the Department of Education on the 17th of this month. A meeting was held on the same day to decide on the principles and steps for the general establishment of remedial classes for all industries, to be implemented in stages. Currently, a white-collar survey is being actively conducted. It is estimated that there are a total of 8,224 factories, companies, and shops in the provincial capital, with a total of 34,455 male and female workers. It is planned to conduct training for workers in the leather-making, printing, rattanware, carpentry, clay work, porcelain painting, sewing, dyeing, hotel, knitting, soy sauce garden, woodenware, and southern goods and dried fruit industries in the early stage. Remedial classes will be established soon. Remedial classes for other industries are also being planned. The Outline of the Implementation Plan for Education in All Industries is attached below:

Outline of the Implementation Plan for Education in All Industries in Jiangxi Province

(1) Significance: In view of the current decline in all industries and economic recession in this province, this province is using educational methods to improve the skills of workers (including shop assistants) in all industries and instill basic knowledge of citizenship, hence the name Education for All Industries. (2) Principles: I. To enable those who have jobs to be proficient in their profession and at the same time enjoy their work. II. To enable unemployed youth who have received vocational training to return to work. III. To use existing specialized talents and equipment to form classes for training. IV. To liaise with relevant agencies for division of labor and cooperation. (3) Supervision and Guidance Agencies: In addition to the Department of Education being the supervisory agency for education in all industries, the provincial government will convene the heads of relevant agencies, industry leaders, and people enthusiastic about education in all industries to organize the Jiangxi Provincial Committee for the Implementation of Education in All Industries (hereinafter referred to as the Committee) to be responsible for investigation, design, and guidance matters. The organizational regulations will be determined separately. (4) Teaching Venues: A. Provincial vocational schools and mass education institutions, and provincial factories should all set up remedial classes for all industries. The subjects and types will be designated separately. B. Factories, companies, shops, etc., with 20 or more employees should set up remedial classes themselves in the factory, company, or shop. Those with fewer than 20 employees should jointly set up remedial classes with nearby businesses in the same industry, using the larger of the jointly established factories, companies, or shops, or the trade association as the teaching venue. However, factories, companies, shops, etc., whose employees have already entered remedial classes in item A do not need to set up or jointly set up remedial classes themselves. After the establishment of the first two types of remedial classes for one month, a form should be filled out and submitted to the Department of Education. The form will be determined separately. Those belonging to item B may request the Department of Education or the Committee to send personnel for guidance when they are established. (5) Curriculum: The curriculum of the remedial classes for all industries is divided into two categories: basic knowledge of citizenship and vocational guidance. The subjects are as follows: A. Those related to basic knowledge of citizenship: General meaning of the Three Principles of the People, Citizen's Guide, Current Affairs Lectures. B. Those related to vocational guidance: Service ethics, vocational knowledge (established according to the needs of each industry), vocational skills (emphasizing the transmission of technology and experience). In the above-mentioned teaching, the principle is that the time allocated to basic knowledge of citizenship accounts for one-third, and vocational guidance accounts for two-thirds. (6) Teachers: A. The teachers of the remedial classes for all industries are hired by the original establishment agency, or the Committee may be requested to select and send them. In addition to hiring from all parties, a teacher registration for all industries will be held. Any person who is confident in their skills in a certain industry and volunteers to be a teacher in the industry can register. The Committee will handle it. B. For those remedial classes for all industries that belong to handicraft guidance, the Committee will handle it jointly with the Handicraft Research Institute of the Bureau of Industry and Commerce. (7) Expenses: A. Items: I. Teacher salaries are standardized at 50 cents to one yuan per hour. II. Material consumption is determined separately according to the nature of the subject. III. Office expenses are limited to necessary lighting, stationery, etc. B. Sources: I. Those affiliated with provincial vocational schools and mass education institutions, and provincial factories, the expenses are budgeted by the respective institutions, and submitted to the Department of Education for approval and paid from the provincial education funds. II. Factories, companies, and shops that set up remedial classes, the expenses are borne by the respective factories, companies, and shops (if they are jointly established by the same industry, the expenses are shared equally by the jointly established factories, companies, and shops based on the number of students), but subsidies may be granted from the provincial education funds. The subsidy standards will be determined separately. (8) Duration of Remedial Classes, Time, and Number of Hours: The duration of remedial classes is determined according to the nature of each industry, ranging from three months to six months. The number of remedial hours per week ranges from three hours to six hours, and the principle is to use spare time for remedial classes. (9) Certificate of Completion of Remedial Classes: After the completion of the remedial classes, a certificate of completion of the remedial classes will be issued after passing the examination by the Department of Education. (10) Guidance for Returning to Work: Young people who have received vocational training and are interested in finding employment or operating their own business but lack the strength may report to the Committee. After verification, appropriate spiritual or material assistance will be provided. (11) Implementation Procedure: First, start with the workers in various industries in Nanchang City. All workers in various industries in this city must receive education. The order in which various industries hold remedial classes will be determined by the Department of Education, submitted to the provincial government for public announcement, and enforced. Once the city has achieved results, it will be extended to various counties and cities. (12) This Implementation Plan Outline shall be implemented after being approved by the Jiangxi Provincial Government.

Tian Bolie Returns to England by Ship, Publishes Letter to Chinese Historians (1) Welcoming China to the International Historical Society

International Historical Society President Tian Bolie, at 8:30 yesterday morning, boarded the Changxing Company's "Queen of Asia" ship to Singapore, en route back to England. Representatives from various cultural organizations in this city, including Kang Xuanyi, Jiang Jianbai, Chen Hongfan, Chen Derong, Lei Guoneng, Li Enshao, and others, went to the port to see him off. Before his departure, Tian also published a letter to Chinese historians, which Kang Xuanyi translated into Chinese and published as follows: "At this critical time, I bid farewell to China, hoping that Chinese scholars will live up to their past reputation. It is especially important to remember that concentrated knowledge can have a great impact not only on the people and nation but also on the entire world. China should demonstrate its position in European and world academic conferences and achieve success through knowledge and scholarship. Previously, at the Beijing YMCA, I listened to a Chinese student English speech contest, which was very interesting. The mouths of these young people were full of nationalistic ideas. They spoke of the sorrows and humiliations of the country and its painful state in the international community, which made me sympathize with the enthusiasm of the youth and recall the era when Germany, a great European power, issued the same lament. Germany was then divided, ravaged, and suffering. The great poet Schiller said to Germany at that time, 'Only one thing can comfort you: though your land is ruled by others, Germany possesses the intellectual world and can still claim supreme status here.' I am neither a poet nor a politician, and as a member of an international organization, I feel it is inconvenient to freely express any preference for any nation or people. But one thing is certain: no country in the world has demonstrated as much in the world of thought and scholarship as China. She absorbs Western scholarship and enriches it with her own immortal traditions. There has been great progress in this regard. I am convinced that if China can adopt the right methods, it can be equal to any country on earth in terms of thought. Politics and war are dangerous games, and their results are often uncertain. The path to success through knowledge and scholarship, although difficult, is assured. China's lofty position in the world of knowledge, once chosen, can be established at any time. It is not enough for China to merely promote and absorb Western scholarship; it should also contribute its own renewed culture to the culture of every country in the world. Every nation should have its national and international aspects. Every nation has something to contribute to creating the honey of international life and achieving the great success of universal science. Every nation is related to the international community, and all who give or take from it will be blessed. I am not now talking about the world of politics, which is indeed encountering difficulties, as you all know. I am talking about the world of thought and knowledge and the world of scholarship, which are so closely related to the noblest traditions of your nation. At this moment, China can join international organizations, and other countries will not only recognize its past contributions but also benefit from its present contributions, and China will also benefit from them. Now, China goes to Europe and the United States to seek Western scholarship and then brings it back to China. But she has not yet fully participated in international academic organizations. Assuming that China has worked hard to save itself in terms of knowledge, it should not only express itself within China; it should not be confined to the Great Wall. It must show its position in European and world academic conferences. Can China do it then? I answer: yes, yes, it can definitely do it. In several knowledge organizations, China's position can be felt. First, Mr. Bonner, Chairman of the International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation, came here several years ago and worked hard to establish a National Committee on Intellectual Cooperation. I know to this day that the association has been helpful to China, and China must know that there is nothing more to hope for from the association than stimulation and guidance. Moreover, on a level plane, it is very difficult to guide literature, art, and science by solitary power. I think in Europe, in fact, there must be a special international organization for each special discipline. (To be continued)"

Shen Bao Medical Journal

The Urgent Need to Rescue and Protect the Soldiers at the Suiyuan Front (Continued)

— A Lecture by Dr. Pang Jingzhou, Recorded by Jiang Huiming

3. Defense Against Poison Gas

The victory or defeat of modern warfare is determined by the quality of military equipment, which seems to be undeniable. But sometimes, it is not that simple and also depends on "heavenly timing," "geographical advantages," and "human harmony." As everyone knows, the most formidable weapon in modern warfare is the air force. The air force's authority can destroy enemy cities and poison countless soldiers and civilians within minutes. Any country that pays attention to national defense is actively preparing and hoping to increase the number of its air force every year. It is conceivable how authoritative the air force is in warfare. Many military strategists even say that the future insecurity of the world depends on the gift of the air force! We often hear these arguments in our ears, and we are constantly worrying about enemy air raids. The soldiers in Suiyuan are naturally very concerned as well.

Since the bloody battles to recapture Bailingmiao, we seem to have experienced that the enemy's aircraft have completely lost their control! Needless to say, this is because heavenly timing and geographical advantages are beneficial to us. We know that when the enemy launches an air raid, releasing poison gas requires the help of wind power. This so-called wind power must have a certain direction and not too strong intensity to achieve its purpose. However, Suiyuan is originally a desert, and the climate is extremely cold, often below minus 15 degrees Celsius. Sometimes, the temperature changes greatly in the morning and evening, so the wind direction is not only uncertain, but the gales are also uncontrollable. The poison gas released by the air raids is not only blown away into the unknown in the air but sometimes even poses a danger of being blown back into its own camp. The impact that the enemy's camp surface can receive is minimal! Therefore, the power of the enemy's poison gas is like a hero with no place to use his skills. At the same time, in Suiyuan, our country, there are few high mountains, only plains, yellow grass everywhere, and no one around. Looking into the night, it is as if the sky and earth are one color. The enemy's aircraft have also lost their explosive power. Even if the enemy's aircraft indiscriminately drop bombs, the chance of being bombed is very small, just like buying an aviation lottery ticket, where it is never certain to win. Because there are very few targets for aircraft to bomb in that area, we are lucky to have the advantage of geography.

Even more excitingly, the soldiers fighting on the front line are all fighting to win national glory, and death has long been put aside. However, we observed that there is still a small concern. Although the enemy's aircraft have lost their combat power, our soldiers cannot help but be somewhat defensive, which cannot be said to have reduced their fighting strength. Therefore, I believe that it is still necessary to be prepared for prevention. Those who support them in the rear should still actively donate anti-poison equipment and cold-weather supplies, such as gloves, cotton quilts, and vests, and transport them to the front to increase their necessary weapons for killing the enemy.

4. Future Rescue and Protection Policies

The war in Suiyuan is a war for the survival of the Chinese nation. Then, the rescue and protection work should be jointly planned by talents with rescue and protection knowledge from the entire Chinese nation. Therefore, public organizations and the Red Cross Society in Shanghai, which are responsible for rescue and protection work, have the responsibility of contacting rescue talents and rescue organizations in various places and concentrating and distributing them. Beiping can also be regarded as the front line of China's national defense. There are many rescue talents in those places, and it is easy to supply the needs of the front line. Therefore, I still need to go to Beiping to discuss close contact. We believe that future rescue work is not a matter for one corner or one place and should be jointly undertaken by the whole country. What the front needs will determine the countermeasures to be announced to the people of the country. As for the detailed methods, due to time constraints, I will make a public report when there is an opportunity.

Finally, I remember that Mr. Yan Xishan and Mr. Fu Zuoyi both expressed to us after the recovery of Bailingmiao that they believed that future victory would depend on the four words "a grieving army will win." We must not be complacent because Bailingmiao has been recovered. We must also think about the future after the recovery of Bailingmiao, and there are still thorns. We must not underestimate the enemy and not brag about our achievements in order to recover other lost territories. These encouragements completely depend on the continuous encouragement and inspiration of the people in the rear, as well as the continuous provision of material assistance. Furthermore, do not think that we should only provide assistance when we win a battle and withdraw our hands when we lose. Victory and defeat are common in military affairs. The brave soldiers on the front line need the spiritual and material greatness given by the people in the rear.

Reporter's Postscript: Because Mr. Pang was suddenly urged to go to Beiping, there was no time to ask him to correct this article. The reporter is responsible for any recording errors.

The Problem of Wartime Rescue and Protection Control (Part 1)

— Hua Xinren

The national fortune is always in a very difficult time. The war in Suiyuan has become tense. The cold winter has arrived, and our soldiers are fighting bloody battles in the frontier. It is reported that the bandit army in Suiyuan has begun to use chemical weapons in its front. At a time when chemical poison gas is killing people, the rescue and protection of soldiers on the front line is an urgent matter. The war in Suiyuan has begun, and our army has occupied Bailingmiao. The fierce cruelty, the casualties, and the painful, dangerous, sad, and disabled conditions must be unbearable. Moreover, in this border area where medicine is backward, the transportation of large quantities of medicines, the collection of sanitary equipment, and the mobilization of rescue personnel are all urgent matters. In recent years, people in the country have studied various issues in response to very difficult times, but no one has proposed a discussion on the issue of rescue and treatment. This is truly regrettable. According to reports, the Chinese Male Nurses Improvement Association plans to unify the rescue lineup (see various newspapers in Beijing on November 20). Revolutionary elder Ms. He Xiangning has recently collected exhibitions of calligraphy and paintings by famous Party and state figures and will use the proceeds to organize a frontline rescue team. This is truly commendable. Prominent figures from all walks of life in Shanghai are organizing a more permanent rescue undertaking committee, and prominent figures from all walks of life are enthusiastically helping. These are all good phenomena. At this time, the government is planning to take control to avoid chaotic steps. The author takes the liberty of drafting this article based on his daily research experience for the reference of the people of the country, and hopes that wise men will not hesitate to correct it.

The main point of the establishment of a health agency by the state is to provide health care services to the people and prevent diseases on weekdays, so-called to seek the happiness of human society. If a national war breaks out, its responsibility is to rescue and treat the wounded and sick comrades in arms. Our patriotic soldiers work hard and serve the country on the battlefield, braving the frost and enduring hunger in the hail of bullets. Injuries and illnesses are inevitable. If there is no appropriate rescue agency to rescue and treat them, the country will reduce its combat capability due to injuries and illnesses, which is quite unfavorable to the war. If the rescue is effective, the wounded and sick can turn danger into safety and quickly return to the battlefield to protect the country. Therefore, the importance of wartime rescue agencies is not only directly related to the soldiers but also indirectly has a huge impact on the future of the country. In recent years, although the world's major powers have stepped up their military expansion, they have also planned for health facilities. The most obvious example is that Japan divides the national health administration into two types: one is "general health," which specializes in providing health care services to the people and is directly under the Ministry of the Interior; the other is "special health," which specializes in planning military health, so-called national defense health, and is directly under the management of the Army and Navy Ministries. When the author returned to China from Japan in August, he drafted an article introducing his observations on the country's health, which I believe the people of the country have seen in the Central Daily News's previous _ academic weekly. Another example is the Italian-Ethiopian War. At the beginning of the war, many Italian soldiers died of illness due to their inability to adapt to the climate and water of Ethiopia. Later, the Italian authorities realized this and sent medical experts to the front to study it, and also ordered male nurses to accompany the International Red Cross rescue team to work together. In the Italian-Ethiopian War, Italy won because of its good military equipment, but it must also be attributed to the country's health and effective rescue. At present, all countries are in this extraordinary period. Foreign enemies are invading, and the people of the country are fighting together. The war on the border has begun, and the recovery of lost territories is extremely urgent. We should plan ahead to prepare for the expansion of the war; otherwise, it will be difficult to cope with it. First, I will state the main points of the government's rescue control below.

It goes without saying that the government should control wartime rescue. There are two principles for its control: one is the concentration of human resources, and the other is the concentration of financial resources. If there is no proper control on weekdays, there will be a shortage of supply and demand, a lack of measures, and the work will be chaotic and unsystematic, making command inconvenient. First, let's talk about the concentration of human resources.

A. Concentration of human resources... Human resources are very important in extraordinary times. At this time, the government should use its talents and strictly and systematically control the organized medical and health groups in order to facilitate command and benefit work. Therefore, a permanent national rescue undertaking committee should be organized in the capital to take overall consideration. The committee should also include social celebrities and those who are enthusiastic about social service to organize it together. The underdevelopment of medical education and health undertakings in our country in the past originated from the fact that the government and the people did not pay attention to health facilities, so the medical giants took the opportunity to manipulate and suppress them in the dark. The so-called sectarianism and exclusion of dissidents were everywhere. Therefore, there was a conflict between traditional Chinese medicine and Western medicine, and then there was the division between the British-American and German-Japanese factions. More recently, there has been a debate between doctors and nurses, and the infighting is a disgrace to our health and medical education. In the future, we sincerely hope that the people will urge the government to adjust it, and we hope that the highest health administrative authorities should be open and aboveboard and accommodate all kinds of talents in order to improve the undertaking. We must not repeat the same mistakes and take sectarianism as the main focus and factionalism as the basis, giving the people a bad impression. This is also a personnel problem in the control of rescue work. The concentration of talents can also be divided into two categories: organization and training. Organization is the driving force for promoting the undertaking. Without organization, there is no system, which can also be said to be no unity. If the internal organization is not sound, the progress of the undertaking will also be hindered. Try to observe the effect of our country's participation in the pre-money rescue in the past. What are the achievements? In a word, there is no effect at all. The author has also participated in frontline rescue work several times and has experienced it personally, so he also has considerable experience in this regard. The reason for the failure is that the government has no control over rescue. There is no overall plan. For example, various civil groups are enthusiastic about public welfare and organize rescue teams to participate in the front line. They lack training on weekdays and have no organization in the pre-money. This is the so-called rabble. Can they maintain it for a long time based on temporary feelings? Therefore, although the Red Cross flag can be seen on the front line, the work gradually falls into a state of idleness and slackness, and opinions often diverge due to personnel problems. This organization is not sound. The supply and transportation of medicines in the rear is not correct, and they are not in contact with the government. This training is not correct. What is the result? All efforts are wasted, and everyone is ridiculed. This war against the enemy is not a local problem. Is our approach to the rescue problem still developing in an abnormal state or should we ask the government to control it? The previous car can be a lesson, and it is not too late to make amends. Fortunately, the authorities have noticed it.

(1) Organization: In order to cope with the future and the current environment, our country should organize a permanent national anti-poison rescue undertaking committee in the capital as soon as possible, which will be led by the government. Its organization should be divided into a dual organization, that is, a general assembly should be established under the provinces, cities, and counties. If people are needed, they can be called together in a few minutes. If there is nothing to do on weekdays, they can do public health and prevention work. This work should be a committee system. In addition to the sanitation agencies and military authorities as ex officio members, experts should be hired to conduct research work. The committee should be divided into various departments, and its organization is as follows.

(1) General Affairs—Specially responsible for the management of documents, finance, general affairs, and matters of the subordinate departments.

(2) Organization—Specially responsible for expanding the association's affairs and the work of various groups and investigation and registration.

(3) Publicity—Specially responsible for writing, speeches, publishing, editing, and information matters. (4) Research—Specially responsible for researching various medical, anti-poison, and treatment matters, and discussing the association's direction.

Page 16

Discussion on the Term "Tropical Diseases" (Part 1)

— Xiaozu

The term "tropical diseases" clearly takes geography as the standard, encompassing all diseases that occur in the tropics. Even world-wide diseases (Cosmopililical Diseases) that occur in tropical areas can be called tropical diseases. Conversely, diseases that are commonly seen in the tropics but occur in cold and temperate regions cannot be called tropical diseases based on the principles of logic. However, for the sake of convenience, people also call them tropical diseases! Let's take an example! For example, malaria is an important character in tropical medicine. However, it can also be found in the far north of Russia!

Good! Manson, in the preface to his famous book Manson's Tropical Diseases, clearly stated, "I take the term 'tropical diseases' as the name of this book, mostly for convenience without considering its accuracy!" The title which I have elected to give to this work, Tripical Diseases. is more convenient than accurate. This sentence came from the mouth of the contemporary authority on tropical medicine, and it can of course be used as a cited document!

In China, a country that is mostly temperate and less tropical, the history of the term tropical disease is not very long. The medical community's attention to it has only been a matter of decades. The general public's understanding of it may be limited to the gentlemen above the level of current common sense. This is a fact that is related to the progress of medical history, and it is also a recent imported product. It is not that I, a kid, dare to underestimate people! What's more, the so-called scientific Western medicine can only be said to be in its infancy in our country. This last-seeded and most naive medical product is, of course, still a stranger.

What deserves our attention and motivates me to move my fingers and pen is the resolution of the Medical Education Committee of the Ministry of Education (I remember that this is a public agency name?). In this resolution, the subject of tropical diseases was listed as one of the compulsory subjects for medical students in the later period. It was once ordered to be followed by medical education institutions above the specialist level across the country, and special lectures were set up. (I only read about this in the newspapers. I don't know much about the truth.) This incident proves the position that tropical diseases occupy in medicine. Secondly, it is necessary to recognize tropical diseases in China. This bill has established the foundation for the future development of tropical diseases in China. The committee members' vision, detailed planning, and firm determination are truly admirable. Here, I offer a small tribute in the form of a nameless soldier's incense! But then again, I suddenly remembered a sage's saying: "If the name is correct, then the words will be smooth." All things need a name, forming the total mark of the static, dynamic, and meaning of all things themselves. If the name is not correct, then not only will the words not be smooth, but I am afraid that we will take the wrong path. In today's revolutionary trend, following the traditional concept of habit and calling diseases that also occur in cold and temperate regions tropical diseases, or at least listing them as tropical diseases, does not seem very reasonable! We need to carefully consider and correct it, and redistribute it. We cannot just follow others blindly and let it pass vaguely. In others, it is an established history and difficult to change. When we are just starting and want to rectify or transform it, it is a perfect opportunity!

Domestic Medicinal Plants (Continued)

— Zhou Mengbai

Three, Morning Glory, *Pharbitis Nil*, Chois.

(Plant) A common annual vine cultivated for ornamental purposes. The petioles are discarded, and the leaves are deeply lobed, with the central lobe elliptical, sharply pointed, entire, and the base expanded. Funnel-shaped flowers emerge from the axils, with the pedicels shorter than the petioles, bearing 1-3 flowers. The capsules are formed by three carpels, shaped spherically.

American Morning Glory, *P. hederacea*, Chois. The leaves are deeply lobed, with the central lobe ovate and the base expanded. The pedicels are short, bearing only one flower.

(Cultivation Method) For the purpose of harvesting seeds for medicinal use, make ridges 2 feet 5 inches wide. In May or June, sow 2-3 seeds every 1 foot 2 inches along the ridges. Allow the vines to creep along the ground. Around November, when the fruits are fully mature, uproot the entire plant and dry it. Then, strike the plants with a pole to separate the seeds, and winnow them in a sieve for selection. Each acre can yield about one *dou* of seeds, weighing approximately 18 *jin*.

(Medicine) Morning Glory Seed, *Semen Pharbitidis*, is obtained by collecting the seeds. There are two types: grayish-white and dark brownish-black. For medicinal use, the grayish-white type is preferred. They are wedge-shaped, 5 mm long, 3 mm wide, with a hard and brittle, wrinkled seed coat, containing a white embryo inside. The taste is mild, like oil.

(Components) The purgative component in the seeds is a resin glycoside called Pharbitin, present in an amount of about 2%. Pharbitinsaure is a glycoside formed by the combination of Methylpentose and glucose in B-Dioxymyristinsaure. The seeds also contain about 10% fatty oil.

(Medicinal Use) It is traditionally said that Morning Glory Seed is effective as a strong purgative. Due to its significant laxative effect, caution is required when using it. The dosage is 1-3 *fen*, taken internally as a powder.

Morning Glory Seed can be used as a substitute for Jalap root. Morning Glory Resin, prepared for this purpose, can also be used as a substitute for Jalap Resin. (Dosage: 0.5-0.7 *fen*.)

Method for preparing Morning Glory Resin: Finely crush Morning Glory Seed, soak it in warm alcohol, then distill off the alcohol from the soaking solution. Wash the remaining residue with water and dry the portion that floats on the water.

The British Pharmacopoeia includes the seeds of American Morning Glory, called Kaladna (Indian local name). It also includes Compound Kaladana Powder (*Pulvis Kaladanae Compositus*) and Kaladana Resin (*Kaladana Resina*).

Example prescription: Compound Kaladana Powder (British Formulary)

Morning Glory Seed 3.0, Cream of Tartar 6.0, Ginger Powder 1.0 - Daily dose 0.6-4.0 *fen*.

Introducing a New Type of Medical Journal (Part 2)

— Fan Shouyuan

Indeed, the current situation in the medical field is almost unchanged from a few years ago; few of the medical publications available can escape the situation I described above, still suffering from being mediocre. Truly popular medical journals that cater to the public are rare, and those that genuinely provide colleagues in the medical field with reading material and serve as a source of intellectual nourishment for practicing physicians are even fewer. However, this new type of medical journal, currently edited by Dr. Yang, can be described as an unconventional and outstanding publication. It is not generally popular; on the contrary, it explicitly states that it is a specialized medical journal for medical professionals to consult. After examining its content, we can undoubtedly confirm that it truly lives up to its name as a specialized medical journal, suitable for general practitioners to read during their leisure time after seeing patients.

The content of this journal is entirely translated from various medical journals from different countries, making it a genuine introductory work. Another distinctive feature is that all of its topics and texts are mostly practical applications, with very little theoretical exploration. Precisely because of this, it is more suitable for general practicing physicians to consult and more beneficial for their practical use. Although medical theory is equally important as practice, and all practice relies on theoretical foundations, it is a fact that general medical texts often consume a large amount of space due to lengthy theoretical explanations. For general practitioners who are busy with their clinical duties, reading such texts is often uneconomical due to time constraints. This is exactly the real situation described in the editor's statement of purpose: "After reading each article, there is often a regret that it lacks practical use." The editor's resolute founding of this journal clearly demonstrates an understanding of this practical situation. He stepped forward to take on this "matchmaker-like" transportation work for the general practitioners who are busy with their clinical duties, so that individuals could browse various medical journals that emphasize theory but lack practical application in the midst of their busy clinical duties, which is uneconomical in terms of time and even practically impossible. However, they cannot afford to miss out on absorbing and consulting the latest medical knowledge that is constantly evolving. His dedication and spirit are truly admirable!

Furthermore, there is another noteworthy aspect in the editing of this journal: in its table of contents, almost all medical specialties are fully covered, including internal medicine, surgery, gynecology, pediatrics, ophthalmology, otolaryngology, dermatology, venereology, urology, etc. Each specialty has several specialized articles. It almost covers all medical specialties. Clearly, the editor's intention is to provide general practitioners with access to various new medical knowledge and techniques from all aspects. Even specialists who specialize in one or two specific fields can find relevant materials to consult. This is indeed a characteristic feature of this journal.

As for its content, the articles are truly novel, and I deeply admire the editor's selection, and the translation is accurate and clear. If the editor can continue to maintain this spirit in the future, I believe that the journal can achieve the goal of making readers "benefit from each article they read" and "benefit from each issue they read."

As for the various highlights within, I cannot elaborate on them one by one due to space limitations. I urge readers to experience them directly for themselves.

After receiving this new type of medical journal, "Modern Diagnosis Translation Series," I felt a sense of relief, as if the editor had helped me repay a debt that I had been owing for several years.

Finally, I must add one more point: although the price of this journal is not excessively high, if the price could be reduced further to increase the popularity of subscriptions, the number of readers would certainly increase. With more subscribers and a wider readership, the effectiveness and development of this journal would become even greater and faster.

In addition to heavily recommending this valuable gift—"Modern Diagnosis Translation Series"—to readers in the medical field across the country, I also see boundless potential for the journal's future! (The End)

Shunde Factory's Wuyang coarse white was successfully traded at 6,716 bags, at 21 yuan 3 jiao. Shi Xin Factory was 1,820 bags, at 21 yuan 1 jiao. Shantou was another 175 bags, at 20 yuan 9 jiao, totaling 8,711 bags sold.

North-South Goods: Hunan Lotus Seeds from Hankou Clash with Shanghai

Hunan lotus seeds have been quite tight in the Hankou market recently, so the assortments do not match Shanghai. For higher quality goods, the Hankou price requires 42-43 yuan. However, this market's trading prices are relatively flat due to weak sales. Hengzhou goods are around 43 yuan, and top-quality Xiangtan is 46-47 yuan. White lotus seeds are scarce both in terms of arrivals and inventory. Shanghai sells at 47 yuan, but transactions are also rare.

Metals: Internal and External Transactions in Metals Suddenly Halt

Since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek was detained by Zhang Xueliang in Xi'an, metal transactions in Shanghai have suddenly become bleak. Both domestic and foreign customers have stopped processing goods, and the industry has also cut off transactions for overseas orders. Therefore, the market situation yesterday was quite deserted. The foreign exchange rate in the market suddenly softened yesterday, so those in this business suffered losses. If the situation does not improve in the coming days, the future of the metal industry may not be optimistic.

Woolen Fabrics: Camel Wool Sales Are Quite Good

Among the domestic camel wool fabrics, those with tight fibers and a price of 1 yuan 1.2 jiao are being heavily purchased by Hankou merchants, who are using them for lining in large-brand clothing. This has led to a sudden improvement in the market. Long-haired camel wool, also known as "Kai Mo Tai Ke Si" (likely a transliteration), is currently quite popular. Many fashionable men's and women's custom-made coats use this material. Those priced around 10 yuan are almost all sold out, and except for a certain company, inventory is also low. Double-sided yellow camel wool is also selling very well, but the market is flooded with Japanese goods, keeping prices low.

Extraordinary Grain Market Created by the Current Situation

Wheat has reached a high price unseen in decades. Flour prices are rising steadily, with forward prices all above 4 yuan 3 jiao. Red sorghum, corn, oil cakes, and sesame beans have all seen extraordinary increases. Only rice prices, except for thin paddy, have remained stagnant for passenger grade.

Flour Price 433

Yesterday, the flour market saw another major disturbance. Due to the reported increase in the price of foreign wheat, with Chicago up 0.3 jiao in the near term and 0.9 jiao in the long term, and Canada up 0.346 jiao. When prices opened, foreign wheat was reported to be up, and the sudden turmoil in Shaanxi led many to expect higher flour prices due to the unrest. Prices for the current month opened relatively flat, only up 0.2-0.3 jiao, while prices for January-February jumped by 0.7-0.8 jiao. However, prices for March-April suddenly jumped to the limit of 0.1 jiao. Public sentiment was agitated by the situation, adding a new factor to the market. By the afternoon opening, the current month and January were still within limits, but prices from February onwards all increased by 0.1 jiao. Therefore, although public sentiment was high, transactions became sluggish. Future developments will depend on the resolution of the situation.

Wheat Price 712

The opening of wheat futures also saw a uniform surge, for the same reasons as above, believing that it would have a significant impact on wheat sources. Therefore, after the opening, prices for all months rose sharply, with near-term prices up nearly 1 jiao and long-term prices up 1 jiao. By the afternoon opening, near-term prices stabilized due to the lack of actual shortages, but long-term prices became tighter due to the shrinking foreign exchange rate, leading to a larger increase. Prices for January to April increased by 0.12 to 0.19 jiao. The highest prices for March and April both reached 7 yuan 1.2 jiao. This record is truly unprecedented in decades. The current wheat market is also very tense. Factories are still actively purchasing, with Shandong wheat opening at 6 yuan 8.5 jiao, followed by 8 jiao and 7.5 jiao. Fuxin, Shenda, and Fufeng purchased 15,000 bags.

Oil Cakes Soar

Yesterday, standard soybean oil cakes changed hands, and outside buyers were even more active. Generally, people were still afraid of unexpected changes, so they were eager to buy. In addition, Dalian telegraph reported a price increase, and it was rumored that international demand for soybean oil had increased. As a result, the closing price of oil rose by about 0.5 to 0.7 jiao. Standard beans rose sharply by 0.11 to 0.15 jiao, and standard cakes also followed suit by 0.03 to 0.05 jiao.

Soybean Oil Prices Even Higher

The soybean oil market situation is inseparable from the influence of Dalian's several sharp jumps. Due to insufficient supply in various producing areas and foreign firms' sales behaving like a whale swallowing the sea, new high prices are constantly emerging in the Dalian Exchange. The disturbances in this city and the current inland destinations of this city all have a need for winter preparations at the end of the year, and the market price is even more likely to rise sharply. Yesterday morning, sales were stagnant because the standard tended to be soft. After entering Dalian, the standard and spot goods sped forward rapidly, and as a result, they soared by 0.9 to 1 yuan. More than 900 pieces of various oils were traded. Peanut oil was also the same, rising horizontally by 0.3 to 0.4 jiao. It is estimated that 1,600 pieces were traded.

Various Grains Are All Expensive

The price of various grains in this city has been subject to a drastic rise in prices created by the world, and the momentum is quite strong. Red sorghum (i.e., sorghum seeds) has already opened at a price of 4 yuan 1 jiao. Green beans have all broken the 5 yuan mark. Corn requires 4 yuan 2.3 jiao, so the soybean market is even more turbulent. Yesterday, Tancheng beans in the market rose by another 0.1 jiao compared to last Saturday, with a price of 5 yuan 9.5 jiao, and 3,500 bags were purchased by oil extraction plants. Xinan Town beans were 800 bags. Although the current factory appetite is not smooth, the trend is tireless. The remaining various beans rose by 0.06-0.07 jiao. The destinations are this street's inland areas and Nanyang Gang, etc., inquiring about 3,000 bags of various beans. The sharp momentum of the sesame market has not stopped. Yesterday, Shashi sesame opened at 12 yuan, a full 0.7 jiao higher than the previous market. Other various sesames rose by 0.03-0.04 jiao. In the general market transactions, there were 1,200 bags of various sesames. Due to the lack of supply of pure goods from foreign firms, no business was done, and the overall trend is upward, certainly not below that of raw goods.

Rice Prices Alone Are Normal

Yesterday, more than 110 boats of rice arrived in the South Market, totaling more than 23,000 stones of rice. Among them, more than 80 boats were thin paddy. The rain was drizzling, and sentiment turned positive. The local sales market was slightly better. The thin paddy bales initially stagnated but then moved, with about 10,000 bales sold, and the prices rose by 0.05 jiao. Middle-quality goods rose by 0.1 jiao. There were only sporadic transactions of thick japonica rice, and the market was stable. Du Yangjian and Yin Bianyuan were all similar. In the North Market, 24-25 boats arrived, but due to the cloudy and rainy weather, there were few transactions, and the market price did not rise or fall much. Passenger grade rice continues to be flat and weak. Because the source of the Yangtze River has been continuous recently, and the pace of consumption has decreased day by day, and more because of the changes in Shaanxi, Henan and Shaanxi have stopped business, there are still about 10,000 bags left. Yesterday's transactions were only about 4,000 bags. In addition to the oil merchants purchasing 2,261 bags of Hunan rice, this street also supplied Jiangxi and Wenzhou rice to about 2,000 bags. There were no other transactions. The Shanghai South Rice Market's sales are the best this year of thin paddy rice, so the market surpasses Zhabei, and because the wharf facilities are complete, transactions were still able to proceed as usual yesterday despite the rain, unlike the calmness of the North Market. However, money in the market was already tight yesterday, and the transaction today may not be as lively as in the past.

Textiles: The Cloth Market is Also Extremely Chaotic; Factories Halt Sales of All Goods; Customers' Purchases Also Adopt a Wait-and-See Attitude

Yesterday, the cotton cloth market situation was such that, with a major incident occurring in Xi'an, the market situation was also extremely chaotic. The morning market's opening price for yarn plummeted by five yuan, an unexpected development. Industry players were of divided opinions. Yihua Factory's 16-pound Five Blessings, Double Elephant, and 14-pound Single Deer Blue Chicken brands were the first to report a price drop of 1.2 jiao. Sales of lightweight coarse cloth continued as before, with a hundred-plus bales changing hands. The remaining goods also saw some small transactions, with sales prices remaining flat, as both buyers and sellers were indecisive and adopted a wait-and-see approach. Before long, the second round of yarn prices jumped up by twelve yuan, and factories immediately halted sales of all goods. Japanese trading houses stopped accepting customer orders from the Hakka consignment houses, causing existing consignment notes and spot goods to suddenly become sought after, with varying asking prices. In the afternoon, the benchmark yarn price gradually fell back down. Japanese trading houses slightly increased the price of fine cloth twill by about one jiao compared to last week's market price and resumed sales. The market situation calmed down slightly, with small transactions increasing by five fen to one jiao per bolt. However, for most goods on the market, factories were unwilling to quote prices, and customers were not determined to buy, causing trading to stagnate, it is said.

Essays

Snippets

— (Chen Tiewu)

Since life is a pre-arranged role on the stage of the universe, in these extraordinary times, one should perform a few more acts of "Xue Rengui's Eastern Expedition" and "Emperor Guangwu's Restoration."

"Shanbo Visits Friends" and "Meeting Across the Wall," such activities filled with romantic interest are indeed unavoidable in life. But with "humans as the cleaver and chopping board, and we as the fish and meat," and with even the stage on which we stand about to be destroyed, survival has become a major issue. How can you leisurely spend your days in the boudoir, living in "love"?

In the vast sea of people, there is no shortage of those who earnestly play the role of Yue Fei: but there are also many who put on painted faces and play the treacherous minister Qin Hui. Fame and infamy are most clearly written in the historian's pen.

The more brilliant the play, the more profound the impression left on the audience's minds. The more heroic and earth-shattering one's life, the deeper the faith one earns from others.

If you want to leave some traces on the short journey of life, you should perk up and perform this play of life.

Early Winter Visit to Longhua

— Weijing

It was a Sunday in early winter. I was walking alone, with light steps, onto Longhua Road.

In this season when the leaves have all fallen, wandering around Longhua, which is famous for its peach blossoms, seems rather pointless. However, I feel that springtime is the time when Longhua flourishes, a time of smugness and arrogance. Only in this season can you see Longhua's true face. I think that admiring a beauty with a thick layer of makeup between bright lights and green wine is not as good as admiring a village woman without makeup, perhaps then you can actually appreciate two or three parts of natural beauty. This is my motivation for taking a look at Longhua under the grip of the cold.

Step by step, I approached Longhua. Like small fists, the branches of the peach trees stood quietly in the orchards along the road. Although in the late spring season, I had seen these peach trees covered in brocade-like red flowers and green leaves, receiving praise from tourists, today I saw their true faces. Their gray-black and cracked bark was so haggard and devoid of life, just like a beauty in the early morning whose face is frighteningly pale. "Peach Blossom Blush," "Beauty's Skull," everything can be viewed in this way.

In the late spring season, Longhua Road is filled with silk robes and carriages, and horse-drawn carts flowing like water. But in this early winter, it is rare to see even one or two tourists. What can be seen along the way are not gentlemen in suits and ladies in high heels. The only things that decorate this lonely Longhua Road are farmers carrying hoes and loads, and peasant women sitting by the fences, mending clothes and breastfeeding. Besides these, there is nothing but the sounds of chickens crowing and dogs barking, birds chirping and hawks calling, mixed with the sound of the Longhua Temple bell, forming a rustic chorus of nature. Although occasionally one or two streamlined cars speed past, they are only occasional, and in fact, not enough to disrupt the wisps of smoke rising from the groves, which weave together to form a beautiful landscape painting of early winter, a landscape painting full of medieval charm.

And so I think, in a few more days, white snow will flutter onto the earth, onto every peach tree, onto the ancient temple, onto the pagoda, and onto the surrounding bamboo fences and thatched huts. The entire Longhua will be completely immersed in silver-like white snow. Its lightly made-up and plainly dressed charm may be more worthy of longing than the expanse of bright red in March and April. But the people of Shanghai like to join in the fun. If anyone goes to Longhua on a snowy day, they will surely be laughed at as a madman. So you only hear people going to Longhua to see peach blossoms, not going to Longhua to appreciate the snow.

I have appreciated Longhua in early winter. But on my way home, I was constantly thinking in my stomach that in a while, when heaven tore down auspicious snow like white catkins, covering the entire Longhua, I must come here again and leave a few footprints, so that the villagers and monks would not be the only ones to fully enjoy the snow-covered scenery of Longhua.

Changing Nests and Mating Luan Birds

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nine: Vowing Loyalty with a Cup of Water, Lamenting in the Green Lamp's Dim Light; Promising Marriage with Golden Rings, Reporting Yearning Through the Red Affairs

Guoqi nodded and said, "Miss Li is repeating herself to clarify matters. It is right to be honest when making friends, and Miss Li's words are also correct." Youmei pursed her lips and smiled slightly, seemingly with a hint of shyness, raised her face slightly towards the ceiling, and asked, "What are your thoughts on this news, cousin? Oh! I spoke too quickly, and asked again. Hehe." Guoqi also smiled, put away his folding fan, tapped it lightly in his palm, putting on a very calm appearance, frowned and said, "It is always unfortunate when young ladies have such things happen. However, I wonder what kind of person Miss Wang's partner is? If they are well-matched, even if the marriage is not of her own volition, it won't be too bad." Youmei said, "Although I don't understand it very well, I heard that that person is studying in Shanghai, is very playful, and studying is just a façade." Cousin, think about it, a frivolous young man, how can that be good? As the old saying goes, a beautiful flower falls into the dung heap, I think Luo Lan will also become a flower fallen into the dung heap." Guoqi smiled and said, "That's too much." Youmei said, "Although I am being a bit harsh, I feel sorry for her and feel that it's more than just that." Guoqi sighed slightly. Youmei smiled and said, "I'm here to get a reply, cousin. Where is your reply?" Guoqi said, "With the little something I sent, there's no need to send a letter... " As he said this, his eyes looked at the desk. Youmei followed his gaze and smiled, "It's still the same small envelope." Guoqi's expression became serious, and he said, "Miss Li, although we don't see each other often, you must understand me. I am not the kind of person who harms others to benefit myself. Since Miss Jiang is already so distressed, if I send her something again, it would imply an advancement in our friendship. At the same time, if our friendship advances, but her marriage is not fulfilling, then I would not be comforting her, but adding to her distress." Youmei suddenly asked, "So, does cousin plan to end his friendship with her from now on?" The tone of her question was slightly raised, and her chest also slightly lifted, indicating a strengthening of her evidence. Guoqi's words were originally spoken very smoothly, in one breath. But at this moment, he suddenly became speechless, simply looking at Youmei, unable to say a word. Youmei said, "Not only that, since Luo Lan didn't avoid suspicion and sent cousin something very precious, why did cousin accept it so calmly and not return the favor?" Guoqi said, "I feel..." After these three words, he couldn't continue, just opened his folding fan and waved it very lightly in front of his chest. Youmei looked at him like that and smiled slightly again. Then she stood up and half-turned her body to look at him, and asked, "Cousin, can I take away this small envelope on your desk?" (110)

Borrowing Longevity and Demanding Longevity

— Nineteen

It is a common practice to borrow longevity from deities. Although this is superstition, people do not regard it as wrong because it stems from filial piety or sincere foolishness. For example, if a father or mother is seriously ill, and the doctors have all given up, the son, having exhausted all human efforts and unable to turn the tide, is driven by filial piety to sincerely pray to the local Earth God, willing to shorten his own lifespan to extend his parent's. This is originally uncertain. Fortunately, if the father or mother is not destined to die, and their illness improves, then they see the acts of offering thanks to the gods with performances and presenting plaques as a matter of course; otherwise, it would be seen as sacrilege, not to be trifled with.

A certain person, Jia, was a devout believer in gods and Buddhas, and the villagers called him a kind person. That year, his mother fell ill, seriously ill, and both Chinese and Western doctors had given up. Jia was truly anxious, so he secretly prayed to the local Earth God—it is said that he even wrote a petition in the underworld—willing to shorten his lifespan by ten years to extend his mother's. Whether it was the deity's divine power or his mother's lifespan was not yet exhausted, her illness gradually improved day by day. Afterwards, the mother and son were naturally overjoyed and wanted to offer incense and present plaques to thank the divine realm. From then on, Jia was called a filial son by the neighbors and relatives, and Jia accepted it without shame!

This happened ten years ago. So, ten years later, how "filial" is this filial son? This filial son, due to marrying concubines, visiting prostitutes, and keeping mistresses, often demanded money from his mother. At first, he coaxed, then he demanded forcefully; if he didn't get his way, he would slam the table and scold, wishing he could punch his old mother to death and be done with it. One day, Jia had a bizarre idea and suddenly demanded that his mother repay the longevity debt. She said, "The ten years of longevity, I have already lived through, how can I repay you?" This filial son then showed her the method of repaying the longevity, saying to first prepare a petition in the underworld to petition the original Earth God, and then remove the plaque. Then the deities would naturally have a way.

To this day, Jia is still clamoring to "demand longevity, repay longevity," and it is unknown when this debt will be settled!
